	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading mw-first-heading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Nobel Prize</span></h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		<div id="contentSub2"></div>
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Prizes established by Alfred Nobel in 1895</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Award</div><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox vevent"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above summary">Nobel Prize</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Prize.png" class="image"><img alt="A golden medallion with an embossed image of Alfred Nobel facing left in profile. To the left of the man is the text &quot;ALFR•&quot; then &quot;NOBEL&quot;, and on the right, the text (smaller) &quot;NAT•&quot; then &quot;MDCCCXXXIII&quot; above, followed by (smaller) &quot;OB•&quot; then &quot;MDCCCXCVI&quot; below." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Nobel_Prize.png/220px-Nobel_Prize.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="216" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Nobel_Prize.png/330px-Nobel_Prize.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Nobel_Prize.png/440px-Nobel_Prize.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="492" /></a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="width: 33%;">Awarded for</th><td class="infobox-data">Contributions that have conferred the greatest benefit to humankind in the areas of <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Physiology or Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Economics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Peace</a>.</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="width: 33%;">Country</th><td class="infobox-data location"><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> (all prizes except the Peace Prize)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> (Peace Prize only)</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="width: 33%;">Presented by</th><td class="infobox-data attendee"><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences">Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences</a> (Physics,  Chemistry and Economic Sciences<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Assembly_at_the_Karolinska_Institute" title="Nobel Assembly at the Karolinska Institute">Nobel Assembly at the Karolinska Institute</a> (Physiology or Medicine)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Swedish_Academy" title="Swedish Academy">Swedish Academy</a> (Literature)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Nobel_Committee" title="Norwegian Nobel Committee">Norwegian Nobel Committee</a> (Peace)</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="width: 33%;">Reward(s)</th><td class="infobox-data">A gold medal, a diploma, and a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize#Award_money" title="Nobel Prize">monetary award</a> of 10 million <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Krona" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish Krona">SEK</a><sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="width: 33%;">First awarded</th><td class="infobox-data">1901<span class="noprint">&#59;&#32;121&#160;years ago</span><span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">1901</span>)</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="width: 33%;">Last awarded</th><td class="infobox-data">2022</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="width: 33%;">Number of laureates</th><td class="infobox-data">609 prizes to 975 laureates (as of 2021<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nobel_Prize&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="width: 33%;">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://nobelprize.org/">nobelprize<wbr />.org</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Nobel Prizes</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">noh-<span style="font-size:90%">BEL</span></i></a>; <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">Nobelpriset</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA" lang="sv-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Swedish" title="Help:IPA/Swedish">[nʊˈbɛ̂lːˌpriːsɛt]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a>: <i lang="no">Nobelprisen</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA" lang="no-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Norwegian" title="Help:IPA/Norwegian">[nʊˈbɛ̀lːˌpriːsn̩]</a></span>) are five separate prizes that, according to <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Nobel#Nobel_Prize" title="Alfred Nobel">Alfred Nobel's will</a> of 1895, are awarded to "those who, during the preceding year, have conferred the greatest benefit to humankind." <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Nobel" title="Alfred Nobel">Alfred Nobel</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Swedes" title="Swedes">Swedish</a> chemist, engineer, and industrialist most famously known for the invention of <a href="/wiki/Dynamite" title="Dynamite">dynamite</a>. He died in 1896. In his will, he bequeathed all of his "remaining realisable assets" to be used to establish five prizes which became known as "Nobel Prizes." Nobel Prizes were first awarded in 1901.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nobel Prizes are awarded in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">Physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Physiology or Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Literature</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Peace</a> (Nobel characterized the Peace Prize as "to the person who has done the most or best to advance fellowship among nations, the abolition or reduction of standing armies, and the establishment and promotion of peace congresses").<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In 1968, <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Riksbank" title="Sveriges Riksbank">Sveriges Riksbank</a> (Sweden's central bank) funded the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize in Economics">Prize in Economic Sciences</a> in Memory of Alfred Nobel, to also be administered by the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Foundation" title="Nobel Foundation">Nobel Foundation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Nobel Prizes are widely regarded as the most prestigious awards available in their respective fields.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shalev8_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shalev8-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The prize ceremonies take place annually. Each recipient (known as a "<a href="/wiki/Laureate" title="Laureate">laureate</a>") receives a gold medal, a <a href="/wiki/Diploma" title="Diploma">diploma</a>, and a monetary award. In 2021, the Nobel Prize monetary award is 10,000,000 <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Krona" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish Krona">SEK</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PrizeAmountRaised_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrizeAmountRaised-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> A prize may not be shared among more than three individuals, although the Nobel Peace Prize can be awarded to organizations of more than three people.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Although Nobel Prizes are not awarded posthumously, if a person is awarded a prize and dies before receiving it, the prize is presented.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc1003_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc1003-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Nobel Prizes, beginning in 1901, and the Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences, beginning in 1969, have been awarded 609 times to 975 people and 25 organizations. Five individuals and two organisations have received more than one Nobel Prize.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Prizes"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Prizes</span></a>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A black and white photo of a bearded man in his fifties sitting in a chair." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg/170px-AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg/255px-AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg/340px-AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1872" data-file-height="2516" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AlfredNobel_adjusted.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alfred Nobel had the unpleasant surprise of reading his own obituary, which was titled "The merchant of death is dead", in a French newspaper.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alfred_Nobel" title="Alfred Nobel">Alfred Nobel</a> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sv-Alfred_Nobel.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/00/Sv-Alfred_Nobel.ogg" class="internal" title="Sv-Alfred Nobel.ogg">listen</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Sv-Alfred_Nobel.ogg" title="File:Sv-Alfred Nobel.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>) was born on 21 October 1833 in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, Sweden, into a family of engineers.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz5_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz5-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He was a <a href="/wiki/Chemist" title="Chemist">chemist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineer" title="Engineer">engineer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Inventor" class="mw-redirect" title="Inventor">inventor</a>. In 1894, Nobel purchased the <a href="/wiki/Bofors" title="Bofors">Bofors</a> iron and steel mill, which he made into a major <a href="/wiki/Weapon" title="Weapon">armaments</a> <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturer</a>. Nobel also invented <a href="/wiki/Ballistite" title="Ballistite">ballistite</a>. This invention was a precursor to many smokeless military explosives, especially the British smokeless powder <a href="/wiki/Cordite" title="Cordite">cordite</a>. As a consequence of his patent claims, Nobel was eventually involved in a <a href="/wiki/Patent_infringement" title="Patent infringement">patent infringement</a> <a href="/wiki/Lawsuit" title="Lawsuit">lawsuit</a> over cordite. Nobel amassed a fortune during his lifetime, with most of his wealth coming from his 355&#160;inventions, of which <a href="/wiki/Dynamite" title="Dynamite">dynamite</a> is the most famous.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz11_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz11-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1888, Nobel was astonished to read his own <a href="/wiki/Obituary" title="Obituary">obituary</a>, titled "The merchant of death is dead", in a French newspaper. It was Alfred's brother <a href="/wiki/Ludvig_Nobel" title="Ludvig Nobel">Ludvig</a> who had died; the obituary was eight years premature. The article disconcerted Nobel and made him apprehensive about how he would be remembered. This inspired him to change his <a href="/wiki/Will_and_testament" title="Will and testament">will</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Time_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> On 10 December 1896, Alfred Nobel died in his villa in <a href="/wiki/Sanremo" title="Sanremo">San Remo, Italy</a>, from a <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_hemorrhage" class="mw-redirect" title="Cerebral hemorrhage">cerebral haemorrhage</a>. He was 63 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-Sohlman13_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sohlman13-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nobel wrote several wills during his lifetime. He composed the last over a year before he died, signing it at the Swedish–Norwegian Club in Paris on 27 November 1895.<sup id="cite_ref-Sohlman7_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sohlman7-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> To widespread astonishment, Nobel's last will specified that his fortune be used to create a series of prizes for those who confer the "greatest benefit on mankind" in <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physiology" title="Physiology">physiology</a> or <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">literature</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peace" title="Peace">peace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thelocal1_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thelocal1-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Nobel bequeathed 94% of his total assets, 31&#160;million SEK (c. US$186&#160;million, €150&#160;million in 2008), to establish the five Nobel Prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams7_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams7-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NobelFoundationPrizeAmount_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NobelFoundationPrizeAmount-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Owing to skepticism surrounding the will, it was not approved by the <a href="/wiki/Storting" title="Storting">Storting</a> in <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> until 26 April 1897.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz13-25_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz13-25-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Executors" class="mw-redirect" title="Executors">executors</a> of the will, <a href="/wiki/Ragnar_Sohlman" title="Ragnar Sohlman">Ragnar Sohlman</a> and Rudolf Lilljequist, formed the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Foundation" title="Nobel Foundation">Nobel Foundation</a> to take care of the fortune and to organise the awarding of prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams7-8_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams7-8-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nobel's instructions named a <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Nobel_Committee" title="Norwegian Nobel Committee">Norwegian Nobel Committee</a> to award the <a href="/wiki/Peace_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace Prize">Peace Prize</a>, the members of whom were appointed shortly after the will was approved in April 1897. Soon thereafter, the other prize-awarding organizations were designated. These were <a href="/wiki/Karolinska_Institute" title="Karolinska Institute">Karolinska Institute</a> on 7 June, the Swedish Academy on 9 June, and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences">Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences</a> on 11 June.<sup id="cite_ref-Crawford1_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crawford1-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The Nobel Foundation reached an agreement on guidelines for how the prizes should be awarded; and, in 1900, the Nobel Foundation's newly created <a href="/wiki/Statute" title="Statute">statutes</a> were promulgated by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_II_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Oscar II of Sweden">King Oscar II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thelocal1_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thelocal1-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1905, the <a href="/wiki/Union_between_Sweden_and_Norway" title="Union between Sweden and Norway">personal union between Sweden and Norway</a> was dissolved.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_Foundation">Nobel Foundation</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation_of_Foundation">Formation of Foundation</span></h4>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Foundation" title="Nobel Foundation">Nobel Foundation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th,_1895.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A paper with stylish handwriting on it with the title &quot;Testament&quot;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg/220px-Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg/330px-Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg/440px-Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th%2C_1895.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2965" data-file-height="2056" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alfred_Nobels_will-November_25th,_1895.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Alfred Nobel's <a href="/wiki/Will_and_testament" title="Will and testament">will</a> stated that 94% of his total assets should be used to establish the Nobel Prizes.</div></div></div>
<p>According to his will and testament read in Stockholm on 30 December 1896, a foundation established by Alfred Nobel would reward those who serve humanity. The Nobel Prize was funded by Alfred Nobel's personal fortune. According to the official sources, Alfred Nobel bequeathed most of his fortune to the Nobel Foundation that now forms the economic base of the Nobel Prize.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Foundation" title="Nobel Foundation">Nobel Foundation</a> was founded as a private organization on 29 June 1900. Its function is to manage the finances and administration of the Nobel Prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz14_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz14-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In accordance with Nobel's <a href="/wiki/Will_and_testament" title="Will and testament">will</a>, the primary task of the foundation is to manage the fortune Nobel left. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Nobel" title="Robert Nobel">Robert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ludvig_Nobel" title="Ludvig Nobel">Ludvig Nobel</a> were involved in the <a href="/wiki/Oil_business" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil business">oil business</a> in <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, and according to Swedish <a href="/wiki/Historian" title="Historian">historian</a> E. Bargengren, who accessed the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_family" title="Nobel family">Nobel family</a> <a href="/wiki/Archive" title="Archive">archive</a>, it was this "decision to allow withdrawal of Alfred's money from <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> that became the decisive factor that enabled the Nobel Prizes to be established".<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Another important task of the Nobel Foundation is to market the prizes internationally and to oversee informal administration related to the prizes. The foundation is not involved in the process of selecting the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_laureates" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel laureates">Nobel laureates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz15_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz15-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feldman16_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman16-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In many ways, the Nobel Foundation is similar to an <a href="/wiki/Investment_company" title="Investment company">investment company</a>, in that it invests Nobel's money to create a solid funding base for the prizes and the administrative activities. The Nobel Foundation is <a href="/wiki/Tax_exemption" title="Tax exemption">exempt from all taxes</a> in Sweden (since 1946) and from investment taxes in the United States (since 1953).<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz17-18_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz17-18-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Since the 1980s, the foundation's investments have become more profitable and as of 31 December 2007, the assets controlled by the Nobel Foundation amounted to 3.628&#160;billion Swedish <i>kronor</i> (c. US$560&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz15-17_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz15-17-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the statutes, the foundation consists of a board of five Swedish or Norwegian citizens, with its seat in Stockholm. The <a href="/wiki/Chairman" class="mw-redirect" title="Chairman">Chairman of the Board</a> is appointed by the Swedish <a href="/wiki/Privy_Council_of_Sweden" title="Privy Council of Sweden">King in Council</a>, with the other four members appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Trustee" title="Trustee">trustees</a> of the prize-awarding <a href="/wiki/Institutions" class="mw-redirect" title="Institutions">institutions</a>. An <a href="/wiki/Executive_director" title="Executive director">Executive Director</a> is chosen from among the <a href="/wiki/Board_of_directors" title="Board of directors">board members</a>, a deputy director is appointed by the King in Council, and two <a href="/wiki/Deputies" class="mw-redirect" title="Deputies">deputies</a> are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Trustees" class="mw-redirect" title="Trustees">trustees</a>. However, since 1995, all the members of the board have been chosen by the trustees, and the executive director and the deputy director appointed by the board itself. As well as the board, the Nobel Foundation is made up of the prize-awarding institutions (the Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences, the Nobel Assembly at Karolinska Institute, the Swedish Academy, and the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Nobel_Committee" title="Norwegian Nobel Committee">Norwegian Nobel Committee</a>), the trustees of these institutions, and <a href="/wiki/Audit" title="Audit">auditors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz15-17_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz15-17-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Foundation_capital_and_cost">Foundation capital and cost</span></h4>
<p>The capital of the Nobel Foundation today is invested 50% in <a href="/wiki/Share_capital" title="Share capital">shares</a>, 20% <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a> and 30% other <a href="/wiki/Investments" class="mw-redirect" title="Investments">investments</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Hedge_funds" class="mw-redirect" title="Hedge funds">hedge funds</a> or <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">real estate</a>). The distribution can vary by 10 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-dn20121202_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn20121202-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> At the beginning of 2008, 64% of the funds were invested mainly in American and European stocks, 20% in bonds, plus 12% in real estate and hedge funds.<sup id="cite_ref-handelsblatt2008_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handelsblatt2008-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, the total annual cost was approximately 120&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Swedish_krona" title="Swedish krona">kronor</a>, with 50&#160;million kronor as the prize money. Further costs to pay institutions and persons engaged in giving the prizes were 27.4&#160;million kronor. The events during the Nobel week in Stockholm and Oslo cost 20.2&#160;million kronor. The administration, Nobel <a href="/wiki/Symposium" title="Symposium">symposium</a>, and similar items had costs of 22.4&#160;million kronor. The cost of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic Sciences">Economic Sciences</a> prize of 16.5&#160;Million kronor is paid by the <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Riksbank" title="Sveriges Riksbank">Sveriges Riksbank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dn20121202_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn20121202-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inaugural_Nobel_prizes">Inaugural Nobel prizes</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%B6ntgen,_Wilhelm_Conrad_(1845-1923).jpg" class="image"><img alt="A black and white photo of a bearded man in his fifties sitting in a chair." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg/170px-R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg/255px-R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg/340px-R%C3%B6ntgen%2C_Wilhelm_Conrad_%281845-1923%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3168" data-file-height="4920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%B6ntgen,_Wilhelm_Conrad_(1845-1923).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_R%C3%B6ntgen" title="Wilhelm Röntgen">Wilhelm Röntgen</a> received the first Physics Prize for his discovery of X-rays.</div></div></div>
<p>Once the Nobel Foundation and its guidelines were in place, the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Committee" title="Nobel Committee">Nobel Committees</a> began collecting nominations for the inaugural prizes. Subsequently, they sent a list of preliminary candidates to the prize-awarding institutions.
</p><p>The Nobel Committee's Physics Prize shortlist cited <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_R%C3%B6ntgen" title="Wilhelm Röntgen">Wilhelm Röntgen</a>'s discovery of <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">X-rays</a> and <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Lenard" title="Philipp Lenard">Philipp Lenard</a>'s work on <a href="/wiki/Cathode_ray" title="Cathode ray">cathode rays</a>. The Academy of Sciences selected Röntgen for the prize.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman134_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman134-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Leroy117-118_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leroy117-118-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In the last decades of the 19th century, many chemists had made significant contributions. Thus, with the Chemistry Prize, the academy "was chiefly faced with merely deciding the order in which these scientists should be awarded the prize".<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz77_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz77-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The academy received 20 nominations, eleven of them for <a href="/wiki/Jacobus_Henricus_van_%27t_Hoff" title="Jacobus Henricus van &#39;t Hoff">Jacobus van 't Hoff</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Crawford118_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crawford118-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Van 't Hoff was awarded the prize for his contributions in <a href="/wiki/Chemical_thermodynamics" title="Chemical thermodynamics">chemical thermodynamics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz81_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz81-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feldman205_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman205-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Swedish Academy chose the poet <a href="/wiki/Sully_Prudhomme" title="Sully Prudhomme">Sully Prudhomme</a> for the first Nobel Prize in Literature. A group including 42 Swedish writers, artists, and literary critics protested against this decision, having expected <a href="/wiki/Leo_Tolstoy" title="Leo Tolstoy">Leo Tolstoy</a> to be awarded.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz144_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz144-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Some, including <a href="/wiki/Burton_Feldman" title="Burton Feldman">Burton Feldman</a>, have criticised this prize because they consider Prudhomme a mediocre poet. Feldman's explanation is that most of the academy members preferred <a href="/wiki/Victorian_literature" title="Victorian literature">Victorian literature</a> and thus selected a Victorian poet.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman69_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman69-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The first Physiology or Medicine Prize went to the German physiologist and microbiologist <a href="/wiki/Emil_von_Behring" title="Emil von Behring">Emil von Behring</a>. During the 1890s, von Behring developed an <a href="/wiki/Antitoxin" title="Antitoxin">antitoxin</a> to treat <a href="/wiki/Diphtheria" title="Diphtheria">diphtheria</a>, which until then was causing thousands of deaths each year.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman242-244_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman242-244-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Leroy233_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leroy233-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> went to the Swiss <a href="/wiki/Henry_Dunant" title="Henry Dunant">Jean Henri Dunant</a> for his role in founding the International <a href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement" title="International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement">Red Cross Movement</a> and initiating the Geneva Convention, and jointly given to French pacifist <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Passy" title="Frédéric Passy">Frédéric Passy</a>, founder of the Peace League and active with Dunant in the Alliance for Order and Civilization.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span></h3>
<p>In 1938 and 1939, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Third Reich</a> forbade three laureates from Germany (<a href="/wiki/Richard_Kuhn" title="Richard Kuhn">Richard Kuhn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Butenandt" title="Adolf Butenandt">Adolf Friedrich Johann Butenandt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Domagk" title="Gerhard Domagk">Gerhard Domagk</a>) from accepting their prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz23_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz23-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> They were all later able to receive the diploma and medal.<sup id="cite_ref-Wilhelm85_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilhelm85-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Even though Sweden was officially neutral during the Second World War, the prizes were awarded irregularly. In 1939, the Peace Prize was not awarded. No prize was awarded in any category from 1940 to 1942, due to the <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Norway" title="German occupation of Norway">occupation of Norway by Germany</a>. In the subsequent year, all prizes were awarded except those for literature and peace.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the occupation of Norway, three members of the Norwegian Nobel Committee fled into exile. The remaining members escaped persecution from the Germans when the Nobel Foundation stated that the committee building in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a> was Swedish property. Thus it was a safe haven from the German military, which was not at war with Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams23_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams23-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> These members kept the work of the committee going, but did not award any prizes. In 1944, the Nobel Foundation, together with the three members in exile, made sure that nominations were submitted for the Peace Prize and that the prize could be awarded once again.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz23_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz23-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prize_in_Economic_Sciences">Prize in Economic Sciences</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG/220px-Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="102" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG/330px-Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG/440px-Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Worldmapnobellaureatesbycountry2.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Nobel laureates by country</div></div></div>
<p>In 1968, Sweden's central bank <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Riksbank" title="Sveriges Riksbank">Sveriges Riksbank</a> celebrated its 300th anniversary by donating a large sum of money to the Nobel Foundation to be used to set up a prize in honour of Alfred Nobel. The following year, the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Sveriges Riksbank Prize in Economic Sciences in Memory of Alfred Nobel</a> was awarded for the first time. The Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences became responsible for selecting laureates. The first laureates for the Economics Prize were <a href="/wiki/Jan_Tinbergen" title="Jan Tinbergen">Jan Tinbergen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ragnar_Frisch" title="Ragnar Frisch">Ragnar Frisch</a> "for having developed and applied dynamic models for the analysis of economic processes".<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman343_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman343-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz207_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz207-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The board of the Nobel Foundation decided that after this addition, it would allow no further new prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz20_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz20-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Award_process">Award process</span></h2>
<p>The award process is similar for all of the Nobel Prizes, the main difference being who can make nominations for each of them.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman16-17_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman16-17-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nominations">Nominations</span></h3><p>
Nomination forms are sent by the Nobel Committee to about 3,000 individuals, usually in September the year before the prizes are awarded. These individuals are generally prominent academics working in a relevant area. Regarding the Peace Prize, inquiries are also sent to governments, former Peace Prize laureates, and current or former members of the Norwegian Nobel Committee. The deadline for the return of the nomination forms is 31 January of the year of the award.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman16-17_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman16-17-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz26_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz26-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The Nobel Committee nominates about 300 potential laureates from these forms and additional names.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams15_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams15-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The nominees are not publicly named, nor are they told that they are being considered for the prize. All nomination records for a prize are sealed for 50 years from the awarding of the prize.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman315_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman315-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/></p><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates#50_year_secrecy_rule" title="List of Nobel laureates">List of Nobel laureates §&#160;50 year secrecy rule</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Selection">Selection</span></h3>
<p>The Nobel Committee then prepares a report reflecting the advice of experts in the relevant fields. This, along with the list of preliminary candidates, is submitted to the prize-awarding institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman52_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman52-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> There are four awarding institutions for the six prizes awarded:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Swedish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences">Royal Swedish Academy of Sciences</a> – Chemistry; Physics; Economics</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nobel_Assembly_at_the_Karolinska_Institute" title="Nobel Assembly at the Karolinska Institute">Nobel Assembly at the Karolinska Institute</a> – Physiology / Medicine</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Swedish_Academy" title="Swedish Academy">Swedish Academy</a> – Literature</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Nobel_Committee" title="Norwegian Nobel Committee">Norwegian Nobel Committee</a> – Peace</li></ul>
<p>The institutions meet to choose the laureate or laureates in each field by a majority vote. Their decision, which cannot be appealed, is announced immediately after the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz25-28_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz25-28-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> A maximum of three laureates and two different works may be selected per award. Except for the Peace Prize, which can be awarded to institutions, the awards can only be given to individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams8_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams8-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Posthumous_nominations">Posthumous nominations</span></h3>
<p>Although posthumous nominations are not presently permitted, individuals who died in the months between their nomination and the decision of the prize committee were originally eligible to receive the prize. This has occurred twice: the 1931 Literature Prize awarded to <a href="/wiki/Erik_Axel_Karlfeldt" title="Erik Axel Karlfeldt">Erik Axel Karlfeldt</a>, and the 1961 Peace Prize awarded to <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">UN Secretary General</a> <a href="/wiki/Dag_Hammarskj%C3%B6ld" title="Dag Hammarskjöld">Dag Hammarskjöld</a>. Since 1974, laureates must be thought alive at the time of the October announcement. There has been one laureate, <a href="/wiki/William_Vickrey" title="William Vickrey">William Vickrey</a>, who in 1996 died after the prize (in <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">Economics</a>) was announced but before it could be presented.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams9_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams9-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> On 3 October 2011, the laureates for the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine</a> were announced; however, the committee was not aware that one of the laureates, <a href="/wiki/Ralph_M._Steinman" title="Ralph M. Steinman">Ralph M. Steinman</a>, had died three days earlier. The committee was debating about Steinman's prize, since the rule is that the prize is not awarded posthumously.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc1003_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc1003-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The committee later decided that as the decision to award Steinman the prize "was made in good faith", it would remain unchanged.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition_time_lag">Recognition time lag</span></h3>
<p>Nobel's will provided for prizes to be awarded in recognition of discoveries made "during the preceding year". Early on, the awards usually recognised recent discoveries.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> However, some of those early discoveries were later discredited. For example, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Fibiger" title="Johannes Fibiger">Johannes Fibiger</a> was awarded the 1926 Prize in <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Physiology or Medicine</a> for his purported discovery of a parasite that caused cancer.<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz125_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz125-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> To avoid repeating this embarrassment, the awards increasingly recognised scientific discoveries that had withstood the test of time.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams25_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams25-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-embo_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-embo-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-scienceline1_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scienceline1-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> According to Ralf Pettersson, former chairman of the Nobel Prize Committee for Physiology or Medicine, "the criterion 'the previous year' is interpreted by the Nobel Assembly as the year when the full impact of the discovery has become evident."<sup id="cite_ref-embo_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-embo-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobelinstituttet_20080913-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A room with pictures on the walls. In the middle of the room there is a wooden table with chairs around it." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Nobelinstituttet_20080913-01.jpg/220px-Nobelinstituttet_20080913-01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Nobelinstituttet_20080913-01.jpg/330px-Nobelinstituttet_20080913-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Nobelinstituttet_20080913-01.jpg/440px-Nobelinstituttet_20080913-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4368" data-file-height="2912" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobelinstituttet_20080913-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The committee room of the Norwegian Nobel Committee</div></div></div>
<p>The interval between the award and the accomplishment it recognises varies from discipline to discipline. The Literature Prize is typically awarded to recognise a cumulative lifetime body of work rather than a single achievement.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The Peace Prize can also be awarded for a lifetime body of work. For example, 2008 laureate <a href="/wiki/Martti_Ahtisaari" title="Martti Ahtisaari">Martti Ahtisaari</a> was awarded for his work to resolve international conflicts.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> However, they can also be awarded for specific recent events.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> For instance, <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">Kofi Annan</a> was awarded the 2001 Peace Prize just four years after becoming the Secretary-General of the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams330_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams330-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Similarly <a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">Yitzhak Rabin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shimon_Peres" title="Shimon Peres">Shimon Peres</a> received the 1994 award, about a year after they successfully concluded the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Accords" title="Oslo Accords">Oslo Accords</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams27_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams27-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The most recent controversy <a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize_controversies#:~:text=2009,-Main%20article%3A%202009&amp;text=The%202009%20prize%20went%20to,%2C%20politically%20motivated%2C%20and%20wishful.">[1]</a> was caused by awarding the 2009 Nobel Peace Prize to <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in his first year as US President.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Awards for physics, chemistry, and medicine are typically awarded once the achievement has been widely accepted. Sometimes, this takes decades – for example, <a href="/wiki/Subrahmanyan_Chandrasekhar" title="Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar">Subrahmanyan Chandrasekhar</a> shared the 1983 Physics Prize for his 1930s work on stellar structure and evolution.<sup id="cite_ref-currentscience_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-currentscience-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Not all scientists live long enough for their work to be recognised. Some discoveries can never be considered for a prize if their impact is realised after the discoverers have died.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Award_ceremonies">Award ceremonies</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:276px;max-width:276px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:100px;max-width:100px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Horbjorn_Jagland_presents_President_Barack_Obama_with_the_Nobel_Prize_medal_and_diploma.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Two men standing on a stage. The man to the left is clapping his hands and looking towards the other man. The second man is smiling and showing two items to an audience not seen on the image. The items are a diploma which includes a painting and a box containing a gold medal. Behind them is a blue pillar clad in flowers." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Horbjorn_Jagland_presents_President_Barack_Obama_with_the_Nobel_Prize_medal_and_diploma.jpg/98px-Horbjorn_Jagland_presents_President_Barack_Obama_with_the_Nobel_Prize_medal_and_diploma.jpg" decoding="async" width="98" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Horbjorn_Jagland_presents_President_Barack_Obama_with_the_Nobel_Prize_medal_and_diploma.jpg/147px-Horbjorn_Jagland_presents_President_Barack_Obama_with_the_Nobel_Prize_medal_and_diploma.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Horbjorn_Jagland_presents_President_Barack_Obama_with_the_Nobel_Prize_medal_and_diploma.jpg/196px-Horbjorn_Jagland_presents_President_Barack_Obama_with_the_Nobel_Prize_medal_and_diploma.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2731" data-file-height="4096" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:172px;max-width:172px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Giovanni_Jona-Lasinio-Nobel_Lecture-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A man in his fifties standing behind a desk with computers on it. On the desk is a sign reading &quot;Kungl. Vetensk. Akad. Sigil&quot;." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Giovanni_Jona-Lasinio-Nobel_Lecture-2.jpg/170px-Giovanni_Jona-Lasinio-Nobel_Lecture-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Giovanni_Jona-Lasinio-Nobel_Lecture-2.jpg/255px-Giovanni_Jona-Lasinio-Nobel_Lecture-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Giovanni_Jona-Lasinio-Nobel_Lecture-2.jpg/340px-Giovanni_Jona-Lasinio-Nobel_Lecture-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1602" data-file-height="1375" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flow-root"><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:;background-color:">Right: <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Jona-Lasinio" title="Giovanni Jona-Lasinio">Giovanni Jona-Lasinio</a> presenting <a href="/wiki/Yoichiro_Nambu" title="Yoichiro Nambu">Yoichiro Nambu</a>'s Nobel Lecture at <a href="/wiki/Aula_Magna_(Stockholm_University)" title="Aula Magna (Stockholm University)">Aula Magna</a>, Stockholm in 2008; Left: Barack Obama after receiving the Nobel Peace Prize in Oslo City Hall from the hands of Norwegian Nobel Committee Chairman <a href="/wiki/Thorbj%C3%B8rn_Jagland" title="Thorbjørn Jagland">Thorbjørn Jagland</a> in 2009</div></div></div></div>
<p>Except for the Peace Prize, the Nobel Prizes are presented in Stockholm, Sweden, at the annual Prize Award Ceremony on 10 December, the anniversary of Nobel's death. The recipients' lectures are normally held in the days prior to the award ceremony. The Peace Prize and its recipients' lectures are presented at the annual Prize Award Ceremony in Oslo, Norway, usually on 10 December. The award ceremonies and the associated banquets are typically major international events.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thelocal2_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thelocal2-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The Prizes awarded in Sweden's ceremonies are held at the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_Concert_Hall" title="Stockholm Concert Hall">Stockholm Concert Hall</a>, with the Nobel banquet following immediately at <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Hall" title="Stockholm City Hall">Stockholm City Hall</a>. The Nobel Peace Prize ceremony has been held at the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Nobel_Institute" title="Norwegian Nobel Institute">Norwegian Nobel Institute</a> (1905–1946), at the <a href="/wiki/Auditorium" title="Auditorium">auditorium</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oslo" title="University of Oslo">University of Oslo</a> (1947–1989), and at <a href="/wiki/Oslo_City_Hall" title="Oslo City Hall">Oslo City Hall</a> (1990–present).<sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz21-23_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz21-23-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The highlight of the Nobel Prize Award Ceremony in Stockholm occurs when each Nobel laureate steps forward to receive the prize from the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Sweden" title="Monarchy of Sweden">King of Sweden</a>. In Oslo, the chairman of the Norwegian Nobel Committee presents the Nobel Peace Prize in the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Norway" title="Monarchy of Norway">King of Norway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_royal_family" title="Norwegian royal family">Norwegian royal family</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thelocal2_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thelocal2-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sweden2_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sweden2-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> At first, King <a href="/wiki/Oscar_II_of_Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Oscar II of Sweden">Oscar II</a> did not approve of awarding grand prizes to foreigners. It is said<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (December 2018)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> that he changed his mind once his attention had been drawn to the publicity value of the prizes for Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_Banquet">Nobel Banquet</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Banquet" title="Nobel Banquet">Nobel Banquet</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobel-banquet-table.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A set table with a white table cloth. There are many plates and glasses plus a menu visible on the table." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Nobel-banquet-table.jpg/220px-Nobel-banquet-table.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Nobel-banquet-table.jpg/330px-Nobel-banquet-table.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Nobel-banquet-table.jpg/440px-Nobel-banquet-table.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobel-banquet-table.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Table at the 2005 Nobel Banquet in Stockholm</div></div></div>
<p>After the award ceremony in Sweden, a banquet is held in the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Hall" title="Blue Hall">Blue Hall</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_City_Hall" title="Stockholm City Hall">Stockholm City Hall</a>, which is attended by the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="Swedish Royal Family">Swedish Royal Family</a> and around 1,300 guests. The <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> banquet is held in Norway at the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Hotel_(Oslo)" title="Grand Hotel (Oslo)">Oslo Grand Hotel</a> after the award ceremony. Apart from the laureate, guests include the president of the <a href="/wiki/Storting" title="Storting">Storting</a>, on occasion the Swedish prime minister, and, since 2006, the King and Queen of Norway. In total, about 250 guests attend.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_lecture">Nobel lecture</span></h3>
<p>According to the statutes of the Nobel Foundation, each laureate is required to give a public lecture on a subject related to the topic of their prize.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The Nobel lecture as a rhetorical genre took decades to reach its current format.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> These lectures normally occur during Nobel Week (the week leading up to the award ceremony and banquet, which begins with the laureates arriving in Stockholm and normally ends with the Nobel banquet), but this is not mandatory. The laureate is only obliged to give the lecture within six months of receiving the prize, but some have happened even later. For example, US President <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Theodore Roosevelt</a> received the Peace Prize in 1906 but gave his lecture in 1910, after his term in office.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams18-19_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams18-19-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The lectures are organized by the same association which selected the laureates.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prizes">Prizes</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medals">Medals</span></h3>
<p>The Nobel Foundation announced on 30 May 2012 that it had awarded the contract for the production of the five (Swedish) Nobel Prize medals to Svenska Medalj AB. Between 1902 and 2010, the Nobel Prize medals were minted by <a href="/wiki/Myntverket" title="Myntverket">Myntverket</a> (the Swedish Mint), Sweden's oldest company, which ceased operations in 2011 after 107 years. In 2011, the Mint of Norway, located in Kongsberg, made the medals. The Nobel Prize medals are registered trademarks of the Nobel Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each medal features an image of Alfred Nobel in left profile on the <a href="/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse" title="Obverse and reverse">obverse</a>. The medals for physics, chemistry, physiology or medicine, and literature have identical obverses, showing the image of Alfred Nobel and the years of his birth and death. Nobel's portrait also appears on the obverse of the Peace Prize medal and the medal for the Economics Prize, but with a slightly different design. For instance, the laureate's name is engraved on the rim of the Economics medal.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman2_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman2-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The image on the reverse of a medal varies according to the institution awarding the prize. The reverse sides of the medals for chemistry and physics share the same design.<sup id="cite_ref-Paulingmedal_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paulingmedal-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Prize_Diploma_Fritz_Haber_1918.JPG" class="image"><img alt="A heavily decorated paper with the name &quot;Fritz Haber&quot; on it." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Nobel_Prize_Diploma_Fritz_Haber_1918.JPG/220px-Nobel_Prize_Diploma_Fritz_Haber_1918.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Nobel_Prize_Diploma_Fritz_Haber_1918.JPG/330px-Nobel_Prize_Diploma_Fritz_Haber_1918.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Nobel_Prize_Diploma_Fritz_Haber_1918.JPG/440px-Nobel_Prize_Diploma_Fritz_Haber_1918.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1938" data-file-height="1296" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nobel_Prize_Diploma_Fritz_Haber_1918.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Laureates receive a heavily decorated diploma together with a gold medal and the prize money. Here <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Haber" title="Fritz Haber">Fritz Haber</a>'s diploma is shown, which he received for the development of a method to synthesise ammonia.</div></div></div>
<p>All medals made before 1980 were struck in 23 <a href="/wiki/Carat_(purity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Carat (purity)">carat</a> gold. Since then, they have been struck in 18 carat <a href="/wiki/Coloured_gold#Green_gold" class="mw-redirect" title="Coloured gold">green gold</a> plated with 24 carat gold. The weight of each medal varies with the value of gold, but averages about 175 grams (0.386&#160;lb) for each medal. The diameter is 66 millimetres (2.6&#160;in) and the thickness varies between 5.2 millimetres (0.20&#160;in) and 2.4 millimetres (0.094&#160;in).<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Because of the high value of their gold content and tendency to be on public display, Nobel medals are subject to medal theft.<sup id="cite_ref-UniversityofCalifornia_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UniversityofCalifornia-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> During World War II, the medals of German scientists <a href="/wiki/Max_von_Laue" title="Max von Laue">Max von Laue</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Franck" title="James Franck">James Franck</a> were sent to Copenhagen for safekeeping. When Germany invaded Denmark, Hungarian chemist (and Nobel laureate himself) <a href="/wiki/George_de_Hevesy" title="George de Hevesy">George de Hevesy</a> dissolved them in <a href="/wiki/Aqua_regia" title="Aqua regia">aqua regia</a> (nitro-hydrochloric acid), to prevent confiscation by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> and to prevent legal problems for the holders. After the war, the gold was recovered from solution, and the medals re-cast.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman397_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman397-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diplomas">Diplomas</span></h3>
<p>Nobel laureates receive a diploma directly from the hands of the King of Sweden, or in the case of the peace prize, the chairman of the Norwegian Nobel Committee. Each diploma is uniquely designed by the prize-awarding institutions for the laureates that receive them.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman2_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman2-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The diploma contains a picture and text in Swedish which states the name of the laureate and normally a citation of why they received the prize. None of the Nobel Peace Prize laureates has ever had a citation on their diplomas.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams18_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams18-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Award_money">Award money</span></h3>
<p>The laureates are given a sum of money when they receive their prizes, in the form of a document confirming the amount awarded.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman2_88-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman2-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The amount of prize money depends upon how much money the Nobel Foundation can award each year. The purse has increased since the 1980s, when the prize money was 880,000 SEK per prize (c. 2.6&#160;million SEK altogether, US$350,000 today). In 2009, the monetary award was 10&#160;million SEK (US$1.4&#160;million).<sup id="cite_ref-Nobel_Prize_Amounts_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nobel_Prize_Amounts-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CNN_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNN-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In June 2012, it was lowered to 8&#160;million SEK.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> If two laureates share the prize in a category, the award grant is divided equally between the recipients. If there are three, the awarding committee has the option of dividing the grant equally, or awarding one-half to one recipient and one-quarter to each of the others.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams8-10_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams8-10-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> It is common for recipients to donate prize money to benefit scientific, cultural, or humanitarian causes.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies_and_criticisms">Controversies and criticisms</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_controversies" title="Nobel Prize controversies">Nobel Prize controversies</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversial_recipients">Controversial recipients</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_A._Kissinger,_U.S._Secretary_of_State,_1973-1977.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Henry_A._Kissinger%2C_U.S._Secretary_of_State%2C_1973-1977.jpg/170px-Henry_A._Kissinger%2C_U.S._Secretary_of_State%2C_1973-1977.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Henry_A._Kissinger%2C_U.S._Secretary_of_State%2C_1973-1977.jpg/255px-Henry_A._Kissinger%2C_U.S._Secretary_of_State%2C_1973-1977.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Henry_A._Kissinger%2C_U.S._Secretary_of_State%2C_1973-1977.jpg/340px-Henry_A._Kissinger%2C_U.S._Secretary_of_State%2C_1973-1977.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2459" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_A._Kissinger,_U.S._Secretary_of_State,_1973-1977.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>When it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kissinger" title="Henry Kissinger">Henry Kissinger</a> was to be awarded the Peace Prize, two of the Norwegian Nobel Committee members resigned in protest.</div></div></div>
<p>Among other criticisms, the Nobel Committees have been accused of having a political agenda, and of omitting more deserving candidates. They have also been accused of <a href="/wiki/Eurocentrism" title="Eurocentrism">Eurocentrism</a>, especially for the Literature Prize.<sup id="cite_ref-Abramsxiv_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abramsxiv-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feldman65_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman65-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sarasota_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sarasota-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Peace Prize</dt></dl>
<p>Among the most criticised Nobel Peace Prizes was the one awarded to <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kissinger" title="Henry Kissinger">Henry Kissinger</a> and <a href="/wiki/L%C3%AA_%C4%90%E1%BB%A9c_Th%E1%BB%8D" title="Lê Đức Thọ">Lê Đức Thọ</a>. This led to the resignation of two Norwegian Nobel Committee members.<sup id="cite_ref-topten_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-topten-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Kissinger and Thọ were awarded the prize for negotiating a ceasefire between <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">North Vietnam</a> and the United States in January 1973. However, when the award was announced, both sides were still engaging in hostilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams219_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams219-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Critics sympathetic to the North announced that Kissinger was not a peace-maker but the opposite, responsible for widening the war. Those hostile to the North and what they considered its deceptive practices during negotiations were deprived of a chance to criticise Lê Đức Thọ, as he declined the award.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman315_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman315-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Abrams315_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams315-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The satirist and musician <a href="/wiki/Tom_Lehrer" title="Tom Lehrer">Tom Lehrer</a> has remarked that "political satire became obsolete when Henry Kissinger was awarded the Nobel Peace Prize."<sup id="cite_ref-Lehrer_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lehrer-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Yasser_Arafat" title="Yasser Arafat">Yasser Arafat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shimon_Peres" title="Shimon Peres">Shimon Peres</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yitzhak_Rabin" title="Yitzhak Rabin">Yitzhak Rabin</a> received the Peace Prize in 1994 for their efforts in making peace between Israel and Palestine.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman315_52-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman315-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz183_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz183-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Immediately after the award was announced, one of the five Norwegian Nobel Committee members denounced Arafat as a terrorist and resigned.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman15-16_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman15-16-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Additional misgivings about Arafat were widely expressed in various newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-Abrams302-306_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams302-306-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another controversial Peace Prize was that awarded to <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> <a href="/wiki/2009_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2009 Nobel Peace Prize">in 2009</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Nominations had closed only eleven days after Obama took office as <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a>, but the actual evaluation occurred over the next eight months.<sup id="cite_ref-philp_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-philp-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Obama himself stated that he did not feel deserving of the award, or worthy of the company in which it would place him.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Past Peace Prize laureates were divided, some saying that Obama deserved the award, and others saying he had not secured the achievements to yet merit such an accolade. Obama's award, along with the previous Peace Prizes for <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>, also prompted accusations of a <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal</a> bias.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Literature Prize</dt></dl>
<p>The award of the 2004 Literature Prize to <a href="/wiki/Elfriede_Jelinek" title="Elfriede Jelinek">Elfriede Jelinek</a> drew a protest from a member of the Swedish Academy, <a href="/wiki/Knut_Ahnlund" title="Knut Ahnlund">Knut Ahnlund</a>. Ahnlund resigned, alleging that the selection of Jelinek had caused "irreparable damage to all progressive forces, it has also confused the general view of literature as an art". He alleged that Jelinek's works were "a mass of text shovelled together without artistic structure".<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> The 2009 Literature Prize to <a href="/wiki/Herta_M%C3%BCller" title="Herta Müller">Herta Müller</a> also generated criticism. According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>, many US literary critics and professors were ignorant of her work.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> This made those critics feel the prizes were too Eurocentric.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The 2019 Literature Prize to <a href="/wiki/Peter_Handke" title="Peter Handke">Peter Handke</a> received heavy criticisms from various authors, such as <a href="/wiki/Salman_Rushdie" title="Salman Rushdie">Salman Rushdie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hari_Kunzru" title="Hari Kunzru">Hari Kunzru</a>, and was condemned by the governments of <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, due to his history of <a href="/wiki/Bosnian_genocide_denial" title="Bosnian genocide denial">Bosnian genocide denialism</a> and his support for <a href="/wiki/Slobodan_Milo%C5%A1evi%C4%87" title="Slobodan Milošević">Slobodan Milošević</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Science prizes</dt></dl>
<p>In 1949, the neurologist <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Egas_Moniz" title="António Egas Moniz">António Egas Moniz</a> received the Physiology or Medicine Prize for his development of the <a href="/wiki/Lobotomy" title="Lobotomy">prefrontal leucotomy</a>. The previous year, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Jackson_Freeman_II" title="Walter Jackson Freeman II">Dr. Walter Freeman</a> had developed a <a href="/wiki/Lobotomy#Transorbital_lobotomy" title="Lobotomy">version of the procedure</a> which was faster and easier to carry out. Due in part to the publicity surrounding the original procedure, Freeman's procedure was prescribed without due consideration or regard for modern <a href="/wiki/Medical_ethics" title="Medical ethics">medical ethics</a>. Endorsed by such influential publications as <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_England_Journal_of_Medicine" title="The New England Journal of Medicine">The New England Journal of Medicine</a></i>, leucotomy or "lobotomy" became so popular that about 5,000 lobotomies were performed in the United States in the three years immediately following Moniz's receipt of the Prize.<sup id="cite_ref-Feldman286-289_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feldman286-289-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overlooked_achievements">Overlooked achievements</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_Gandhi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Portrait_Gandhi.jpg/170px-Portrait_Gandhi.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Portrait_Gandhi.jpg/255px-Portrait_Gandhi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Portrait_Gandhi.jpg/340px-Portrait_Gandhi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2024" data-file-height="3040" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_Gandhi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a>, although nominated five times, was never awarded a Nobel Peace Prize.</div></div></div>
<p>Although <a href="/wiki/Mahatma_Gandhi" title="Mahatma Gandhi">Mahatma Gandhi</a>, an icon of <a href="/wiki/Nonviolence" title="Nonviolence">nonviolence</a> in the 20th century, was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> five times, in 1937, 1938, 1939, 1947, and a few days before he was assassinated on 30 January 1948, he was never awarded the prize.<sup id="cite_ref-Gandhi_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gandhi-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Levinovitz181-186_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levinovitz181-186-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nobel_Also_Rans_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nobel_Also_Rans-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1948, the year of <a href="/wiki/Gandhi%27s_death" class="mw-disambig" title="Gandhi&#39;s death">Gandhi's death</a>, the Norwegian Nobel Committee decided to make no award that year on the grounds that "there was no suitable living candidate".<sup id="cite_ref-Gandhi_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gandhi-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Abrams147-148_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abrams147-148-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1989, this omission was publicly regretted, when the <a href="/wiki/14th_Dalai_Lama" title="14th Dalai Lama">14th Dalai Lama</a> was awarded the Peace Prize, the chairman of the committee said that it was "in part a tribute to the memory of Mahatma Gandhi".<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
